RE: Robert Prince as Administrator of the Estate of Betty Prince v.. Norton

Hospitals, Inc. Jefferson Circuit Court, No. 21-Cl-003709

Dear Records Custodian:

Please find enclosed a subpoena duces tecum and records certification page from Defendant Norton Hospital in the above-referenced action. These are being sent to you in order to obtain a complete certified copy of your entire medical record, including ALL radiology films and billing statements, on Betty Prince, DOB: [DOB-1], who is the Plaintiff in the above- referenced lawsuit. Time reference for request is [DOB-1] to current.

In accordance with the Health Information Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations CFR §164.512(e)(1)(iii), the above-referenced patient has been provided written notice of the issuance of this subpoena, This written notice, a copy of which is attached hereto: 1) contained sufficient information about the above-referenced litigation to allow the Plaintiff to bring an objection; and 2) provided a time period during which an objection should be raised. No objection has been raised. By virtue of the foregoing, this Defendant is making reasonable assurances that Betty Prince and her counsel have, in accordance with HIPAA, been afforded an opportunity to object to the issuance of this subpoena and have not done so.

Please send the certified copy to my attention at the Louisville address listed below and invoice us-for any charges related to processing this request. If pre-payment is required, please fax or mail an invoice to my attention at our Louisville office. If the copy charges are greater than $100.00, please call for authorization. PLEASE CERTIFY THE RECORDS BY EXECUTING THE ENCLOSED RECORDS CERTIFICATION FORM. If you do not have any records for this patient, please indicate on this correspondence and fax it back to [PHONE-1039]. If you do not have access to a notary, please have your signature witnessed by two people.

Please do not hesitate to contact me if you have any questions regarding this request. You may reach me at [PHONE-3]. Thank you in advance for your assistance with this request.

Sincerely,

Anthony Luken Paralegal

* Ok Ok Ok ok ok Ok *

In accordance with the Health Information Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR § 164.512 (e), please take notice that the following medical records regarding Betty Prince, who is the plaintiff in the above-styled action, will be requested via

subpoena duces tecum from the following providers:

Caretenders;

King’s Daughters’ Health- Trimble County Medical Building; King’s Daughters’ Health;

Kentuckiana Cardiovascular Specialists;

University of Louisville Physicians Vascular Surgery; Kindred at Home;

American Kidney Center;

Walmart Pharmacy; and

Bluegrass Kidney Consultants.

OwoNAUMRWNT

Please ‘take notice that the plaintiff has until the close of business on October 5, 2021, in which to file an objection with the Court or otherwise notify undersigned counsel in writing of any objections to this Notice of Intent. If you do not notify us of your objection, we will move forward on October 6, 2021, and send subpoena duces tecum to the custodians of the above-

referenced medical providers to obtain Betty Prince’s medical records.

A copy of this Notice will! be sent to each provider along with the subpoena as

satisfactory assurance that all parties have been placed on notice and afforded an opportunity to




object to the subpoena, Should an objection be made, the party making the objections is

requested to send that objection directly to the provider listed above, with a copy to all counsel.

Respectfully submitted,

/s/ Joseph M. Effinger Joseph M. Effinger

This agreement for treatment between myself (the undersigned patient) and my healthcare provider at King’s Daughters’ Health is to establish clear conditions and consent for the prescription of pain controlling opioid medications or other controlled substances prescribed. Opioid medications are prescribed only for the purpose of treating pain. Other medical care may be prescribed in addition to medications to improve the ability to do daily activities. This may include exercise, use of non-opioid analgesics, physical therapy, psychological evaluation/counseling, weight management, and other beneficial therapies or treatment. | agree to and accept the following conditions for management of the pain medications prescribed by my healthcare provider. Failure to comply with the conditions of this agreement may result in medications being discontinued or possible termination of the healthcare provider /patient relationship. In this event, | understand that | will have 30 days to find a new healthcare provider. | understand that a reduction in the intensity of'my pain AND improvement in my daily life functions is a part of the goals of the treatment. Should it become evident that these goals are not being met, | understand the medications may be weaned or discontinued. | agree to the following:

1. 1 must comply with the following guidelines:

a. | will only use these medications-for the purpose of pain control.

b. I will take the prescribed medications only at the dose and frequency prescribed.

c. | will not increase or change the dose or frequency without consulting my healthcare provider first.

d. If! use any medication at a faster rate than prescribed, | will be without medication for a period of time and this could result in dependence withdrawal that is uncomfortable and may include an uneasy feeling, increased pain, irritability, belly pain, diarrhea, sweats, and serious physical or physiological effects.

e. EARLY refills will not be given.

f. | understand that refills may take up to three business days to process from the time of notification. o,

g. will not attempt to get pain medication or any contro!led substance from any other healthcare provider.

h. will inform all other healthcare providers (ER, surgeon, dentist, etc.) that I am receiving pain medications from my healthcare provider. Should ! receive any other prescriptions for pain medication, | will inform my healthcare provider of the exact medication | received by the next business day.

i. 1am expected to keep scheduled office appointments and understand that | will be required to see my healthcare provider at least every three months for chronic pain management exclusively (all other chronic or acute conditions will be addressed in a separate office visit.) | will obtain all medications from one pharmacy.

k. | will consent to random drug screening at my healthcare provider's request. Unexpected results may result in changing or discontinuing my medications and dismissal from the practice.

Today, she reports that she is actually having hypoglycemic episodes with blood sugars in the 50's approximately three times weekly. Low blood sugar episodes typically occur around dinner time. She sometimes uses only 40 or 45 units of night time insulin rather than her scheduled 55 units secondary to the low blood sugars. Discussion regarding her premeal insulin use reveals that she is using the insulin approximately every four hours rather than before an actual meal. Admits that she typically does not eat breakfast, but she is still using 25 units of short acting insulin two times before her evening meal and a third time at dinner. Enclosure

In-Home Health and Well-being Assessment (IHWA) FAQs

Q1. What is an in-home health and well-being assessment (IHWA)?

Al. An IHWA is a 45 to 90 minute home visit that provides a comprehensive view of your patient's health. It can give you insight into your patient's living situation, medications and health conditions.

An [HWA includes:

Brief exams, including vital signs

Review of active/inactive/chronic medical diagnoses with associated medication Functional status and fall risk assessment

Personal and social history; drug, tobacco and alcohol screenings

Diabetes and cancer assessments

Depression screenings(PHQ) and mental status exam (Mini-Cog)

Clinician assessment of the patient with recommendations

Preventive and chronic disease care recommendations

Case management referral (if applicable)

An IHWA does not:

Replace any regular visit or the annual wellness exam Order or perform any invasive tests/procedures or prescribe medication Carry any additional cost to you or your patient

Q2. What is the value of an IHWA? A2. in-home visits provide an opportunity to:

Learn more about your patient's home environment

Offer information to help you guide your patient to appropriate disease-management programs

Provide a comprehensive view of your patient's medications

Summarize all diagnoses and offer recommendations to your patient for follow- up care

Q3. Where can | learn more?

A3. For assistance, please contact the Humana Provider Call Center at

1-[PHONE-647], Monday through Friday, 8 a.m. to 6 p.m. local time. You also can contact Your Home Advantage at [PHONE-648] Monday through Friday 9 a.m. to 5 p.m. Eastern time.

The purpose of this agreement is to prevent misunderstandings about certain medicines you will be taking for pain management. This is to help both you and your doctor/advanced practice nurse (APN) to comply with the law regarding controlled pharmaceuticals.

| understand that this agreement is essential to the trust and confidence necessary ina provider/patient relationship and that my doctor/APN undertakes to treat me based on this agreement. ,

| understand that if | would break this agreement, my doctor/APN will stop prescribing these pain-controlling medicines, as well as other controlled medicines.

In this case, my doctor/APN will taper off the medication over a period of several days, as necessary, to avoid withdrawal symptoms. Also, a drug-dependence treatment program may be recommended. | will communicate fully with my doctor/APN about the character and intensity of my pain, the effects of the pain on my daily life, and how well the medication is helping to relieve the pain.

| will not use any illegal controlled substances, such as marijuana, cocaine, methamphetamine, etc. { will not share, sell or trade my medications with anyone.

| will not attempt fo obtain any controlled medications, including opioid pain medications, controlled stimulants, or anti-anxiety medications from any other doctor/APN.

| will safeguard my pain medication from loss or theft. Lost or stolen medications will not be replaced.

| agree that refills of my prescriptions for pain medications will be made only at the time ‘of an office visit or during regular office hours. No refills will be available during evenings or on weekends.

{ agree that! will submit to a blood or urine test if requested by my doctor/APN to determine my compliance with my program of pain control medications. Furthermore, | understand that tampering with the drug testing sample constitutes failure of the test and therefore is a break in this agreement. | agree that | will use my medications at a rate no greater than the prescribed rate and that use of my medications at a greater rate will result in my being without medications for a period of time.

| will bring atl unused pain medications to every office visit.

| agree to follow these guidelines that have been fully explained to me. All of my questions and concerns regarding treatment have been adequately answered. A copy of this document has been

given to me. oo o lagree touse: \Nalmaeqs Pharmacy, located at Mads on

telephone number , for filling prescriptions for all my pain medications.

| authorize my doctor/APN and my pharmacy to cooperate fully with law enforcement agencies, including the state’s Board of Pharmacy, in the investigation of any possible misuse, sale, or other diversion of my pain medication. | authorize my doctor/APN to provide a copy of this agreement to

my phafmacy. | agree to waive any applicable privilege or right of privacy or confidentiality with respect to these authorizations. Additionally, | acknowledge that | will no longer be seen by

* A1c 7.9, meaning average blood sugar of 180 over the past 3-4 months. Goal A‘1c for diabetes is <7.

Check fasting (in the morning, before eating or drinking) blood sugar. If >120 for 3 days in a row, increase night-time long acting Insulin by 3 units. Continue to do this until fasting blood sugars are routinely <120.

The purpose of this agreement is to prevent misunderstandings about certain medicines you will be taking for pain management This is to help both you and your doctorfadvanced practice Nurse (APN) to comply with the law regarding controlled pharmaceuticals.

| understand that this agreement ts essential to the trust and confidence necessary ina provider/patent relationship and that my doctor/APN undertakes to treat me based on this agreement.

| understand that if | would break this agreement, my doctor/APN will stop prescribing these pain-controlling medicines, as well as other controlled medicines.

in this case, my doctor/APN will taper off the medication over a period of several days, as necessary, to avoid withdrawal symptoms. Also, a drug-dependence treatment program may be recommended. | will communicate fully with my doctor/APN about the character and intensity of my pain, the effects of the pain on my daily life, and how well the medication is helping to relieve the pain. ;

1 will not use any illegal controlled substances, such as marijuana, cocaine, methamphetamine, etc. | will not share, sell or trade my medications with anyone.

1 will not attempt to obtain any controlled medications, including opioid pain medications, controlled stimulants, of anti-anxiety medications from any other doctor/APN.

| will safeguard my pain medication from loss or theft. Lost or stolen medications will not be replaced

{ agree that refills of my prescriptions for pain medications will be made only at the time of an office visit or during regular office hours. No refills will be available during evenings or on weekends.

| agree that! will submit to a blood or urine test if requested by my doctor/APN to determine my comphance with my program of pain control medications. Furthermore, | understand that tampering with the drug testing sample constitutes failure of the test and therefore is a break in this agreement. | agree that ! will use my medications at a rate no greater than the prescribed rate an that use of my medications at a greater rate will result in my being without medications for a period of time.

| will bring all unused pain medications to every office visit.

1 agree to follow these guidelines that have been fully explained to me All of my questions and concerns regarding treatment have been adequately answered. A copy of this document has been given to me. .

| agree to use: Woke Mae Pharmacy, located at

telephone number ____ for filling prescriptions for all my pain mediaations.

1 authorize my doctor/APN and my pharmacy to cooperate fully with Jaw enforcement agencies, including the state’s Board of Pharmacy, in the investigation of any possible misuse,jsale, or other diversion of my pain medication | authorize my doctor/APN to provide a copy of thig agreement to my pharmacy. | agree to waive any applicable privilege or right of privacy or confid ntiality with respect to these authorizations. Additionally, |! acknowledge that 1 will no longer be seen by oe if | break this contract.

SHOULDER JOINT INJECTION: left

Risks including skin depigmentation, atrophy, and bruising, intra-articular bleeding and infection, tendon weakening or rupture, hyperglycemia, osteopenia, and increased pain post-injection are discussed. Benefits of increased range of motion and improved pain control are discussed. Alternative therapies of oral pain medication and physical therapy exercises are offered. Patient voices understanding of these risks, benefits, and alternatives and gives verbal consent to proceed with the joint injection.

Skin is prepped with Betadine swabstick x2 and alcohol. Coracoid process is sterilely palpated and 22-gauge, 1-1/2 inch needle, is inserted 1/2 inch below the coracoid process and is directed outward toward the medial portion of the humeral head. A mixture of 3 mL of 1% lidocaine without epinephrine and 1 mL of Kenalog 40 mg is injected into the joint space without complication. Band-Aid is applied over the injection site.

Post-injection, passive full range of motion of the shoulder joint is demonstrated. Patient denies numbness or tingling in the arm or hand. Patient is instructed to call me if swelling, redness, warmth, fever, or numbness/tingling develop.

Submitted prescription for Levemir. Discontinued prescription for Lipitor.




The purpose of this agreement is to prevent misunderstandings about certain medicines you will be taking-for pain. management. This.is.to help both you and your provider to comply with the law- ~ regarding controlled pharmaceuticals.

| understand that this agreement is essential to the trust and confidence necessary in a orovider/patient relationship and that my provider undertakes to treat me based on this agreement.

| understand that if | would break this agreement, my provider will stop prescribing these pain-controlling medicines, as well as other controlled medicines.

In this case, my provider will taper off the medication over a period of several days, as necessary, to avoid withdrawal symptoms. Also, a drug-dependence treatment program may be recommended.

| will communicate fully with my provider about the character and intensity of my pain, the effects of the pain on my daily life, and how well the medication is helping to relieve the pain.

| will not use any illegal controlled substances, such as marijuana, cocaine, methamphetamine, etc. | will not share, sell or trade my medications with anyone.

| will not attempt to obtain any controlled medications, including opioid pain medications, controlled stimulants, or anti-anxiety medications from any other provider.

| will safeguard my pain medication from loss or theft. Lost or stolen medications will not be replaced.

| agree that refills of my prescriptions for pain medications will be made only at the time of an office visit or during regular office hours. No refills will be available during evenings or on weekends.

| agree that I will submit to a blood or urine test if requested by my provider to determine my compliance with my program of pain control medications. Furthermore, ! understand that tampering with the drug testing sample constitutes failure of the test and therefore is a break in this agreement. i agree that | will use my medications at a rate no greater than the prescribed rate and that use of my medications at a greater rate will result in my being without medications for a period of time.

| will bring all unused pain medications to every office visit.

SHOULDER JOINT INJECTION: L shoulder

Risks including skin depigmentation, atrophy, and bruising, intra-articular bleeding and infection, tendon weakening or rupture, hyperglycemia, osteopenia, and increased pain post-injection are discussed. Benefits of increased range of motion and improved pain control are discussed. Alternative therapies of oral pain medication and physical therapy exercises are offered. Patient voices understanding of these risks, benefits, and alternatives and consents to proceed with the joint injection.

Skin is prepped with Betadine swabstick x2 and alcohol. Coracoid process is sterilely palpated and 22-gauge, 1-1/2 inch needle, is inserted 1/2 inch below the coracoid process and is directed outward toward the medial portion of the

humeral head. A mixture of 3 mL of 1% lidocaine without epinephrine and 1 mL of Kenalog 40 mg is injected into the joint space without complication. Band-Aid is applied over the injection site.

PRINCE,BETTY MAE [DOB-918] 4 of 4




The purpose of this agreement is to prevent misunderstandings about certain medicines you will be — ~ taking-for pain management. This-is to. help both-you and- Your provider to-comply-with the law-——:- regarding controlled pharmaceuticals.

| understand that this agreement is essential to the trust and confidence necessary in a provider/patient relationship and that my provider undertakes to treat me based on this agreement.

| understand that if! would break this agreement, my provider will stop prescribing these pain-controlling medicines, as well as other controlled medicines.

In this case, my provider will taper off the medication over a period of several days, as necessary, to avoid withdrawal symptoms. Also, a drug-dependence treatment program may be recommended.

| will communicate fully with my provider about the character and intensity of my pain, the effects of the pain on my daily life, and how well the medication is helping to relieve the pain.

| will not use any illegal controlled substances, such as Marijuana, cocaine, methamphetamine, etc.

| will not share, sell or trade my medications with anyone.

[ will not attempt to obtain any controlled medications, includin Stimulants, or anti-anxiety medications from any other provider. | will safeguard my pain medication from loss or theft. Lost or stolen medications will not be replaced. .

f agree that refills of my prescriptions for pain medications will be made only at the time of an office visit or during regular office hours. No refills will be available during evenings or on weekends.

The purpose of this agreement is to prevent misunderstandings about certain medicines you will be — ~ taking-for pain management. This-is to. help both-you and- Your provider to-comply-with the law-——:- regarding controlled pharmaceuticals.

| understand that this agreement is essential to the trust and confidence necessary in a provider/patient relationship and that my provider undertakes to treat me based on this agreement.

| understand that if! would break this agreement, my provider will stop prescribing these pain-controlling medicines, as well as other controlled medicines.

In this case, my provider will taper off the medication over a period of several days, as necessary, to avoid withdrawal symptoms. Also, a drug-dependence treatment program may be recommended.

| will communicate fully with my provider about the character and intensity of my pain, the effects of the pain on my daily life, and how well the medication is helping to relieve the pain.

| will not use any illegal controlled substances, such as Marijuana, cocaine, methamphetamine, etc.

| will not share, sell or trade my medications with anyone.

[ will not attempt to obtain any controlled medications, includin Stimulants, or anti-anxiety medications from any other provider. | will safeguard my pain medication from loss or theft. Lost or stolen medications will not be replaced. .

f agree that refills of my prescriptions for pain medications will be made only at the time of an office visit or during regular office hours. No refills will be available during evenings or on weekends.

| agree that | will submit to a blood or urine test if requested by my provider to determine my compliance with my program of pain control medications. Chief Complaint Pulled muscle in her lower back over the weekend.

History of Present Illness

Betty comes in today complaining that she has been having pain in the left side of her lower back since this weekend. She bent down to pick up a heavy bag of groceries and felt a pulling in the left side of her back. She says that since then she has been sore, having trouble mostly getting up and down from a seated position or if she is trying to do a lot of twisting or bending she will have pain in her lower back. She hasn't taken anything OTC because she was recently diagnosed with some chronic renal insufficiency and doesn't know what to take. She had a GFR of 30 on the 25th of February. Medication adjustments were made at that time. She denies presently that she is having any leg numbness, tingling or weakness. No bowel or bladder dysfunction. No dysuria or hematuria. She is breathing fine. No pleuritic pain or cough. She hasn't put ice or heat on her back, either, because she wasn't sure which one to use. Denies that she has had any rash there.

PFSH

Past medical and social history is reviewed.

Review of Systems As in HPI.

Examination

GENERAL: Well appearing, alert, cooperative. No acute distress.

HEENT: PERRL. Conjunctivae are clear. Oropharynx is clear.

NECK: Without adenopathy.

CARDIAC: Regular rate and rhythm without murmur, rub or gallop.

LUNGS: Clear to auscultation without wheeze, rhonchi or crackle.

MUSCULOSKELETAL: Significant for normal appearing spine. No tenderness along the spine itself. She does have some mild tenderness along the left lumbar paravertebrals but no palpable spasm. She has decreased range of motion with forward flexion limited to about 45 degrees. Neurologically, patellar reflexes are 2+. Strength is 5/5 in lower extremities including dorsi and plantar flexion.

Assessment/Plan 1. Left lumbar strain.

| did advise Betty that we will treat her symptomatically with Robaxin 750 mg q8h prn as a muscle relaxer. She was also advised to use ice in 10-15 minute increments and that she may take OTC Tylenol 1,000 mg four times daily but she should avoid any anti-inflammatory products. | did give her some samples of Tylenol here today. She is also prescribed Tramadol 50 mg g8h prn severe pain, #30 with no additional refills. She will let me know if she has worsening symptomatology.

Today's Orders

5/3/10 PRINCE,BETTY M [DOB-1005] 1 of 3




Chief Complaint 1. Discuss medication changes. 2. Wants an injection in her left shoulder.

History of Present Illness

Betty comes in today to go over some recent labs and several of her medications that were changed. She did have blood work on the 25th of February and was noted to have some decrease in her GFR from 37 down to 30. Secondary to this, | discontinued her Zantac and Atenolol or Chlorthalidone. The Atenolol was replaced with Carbetolol. She was also given some instruction to decrease several of her medications to 1/2 doses due to the renal insufficiency. This included decreasing her Januvia, Metformin and Lotensin. Secondary to the decrease in these medications, we had given her some instructions over the phone regarding her insulin but she was concerned about all of the changes and wanted to make an appointment to discuss.

She also would like to get another steroid injection in her left shoulder. She has some osteoarthritis. She had a Kenalog injection in June of 2012 and felt like that worked very well and wonders if she can get another one because she is starting to get some stiffness again. She is not on any chronic anti-inflammatory medicine secondary to her renal function. She says that she really doesn't have to do a whole lot of activity but does notice the shoulder aching and stiffening up on her especially if she wants to do something over her head or if she tries to reach behind her. PFSH

Past medical and social history are reviewed and updated.

Review of Systems As in HPI.

Examination

GENERAL: Well appearing, alert, cooperative. No acute distress.

HEENT: PERRL. Conjunctiva are clear. Nares are clear.

MUSCULOSKELETAL: Significant for examination of her left shoulder. She has no obvious visible deformity. She does have some tenderness to palpation along the acromioclavicular joint as well as anteriorly. She has fair range of motion of the shoulder but some pain with range of motion above about 120 degrees.

Assessment/Plan 1. Left shoulder osteoarthritis.

| did inject Ms. Prince's shoulder today with Kenalog 40 mg and Lidocaine without Epinephrine 1 ml. This was done under sterile technique and she tolerated the procedure well.

2. Chronic renal insufficiency with some acute worsening.

Again, we did recommend medication changes including discontinuation of her Zantac and Atenolol Chlorthalidone as well as decreasing her Januvia, Metformin and Lotensin. She is further reminded to avoid OTC anti- inflammtories.

3. Hypertension.

| did add on Carvedilol 12.5 mg twice daily to account for the discontinuation of the Atenolol.

4. Insulin dependent diabetes.

| did go ahead and increase her Lantus up to 70 units nightly and gave her detailed instructions today on titrating that by three units every three days until her fasting blood sugars are less than 100.

Today's Orders

Plan: Prescriptions

Chief Complaint

Follow up for medication refills and labs.

History of Present Illness

Betty comes in today for routine follow up of her chronic medical issues which include hypertension, hypercholesterolemia. coronary artery disease and type 2 diabetes. She is on multiple blood pressure medications including Norvasc, Benazepril and Atenolol with diuretic. She does check her blood pressures at home and says they are always a little lower than they are here. It seems like it's always elevated when she comes to the doctor. Her blood pressure last visit was in the 150's/70 range as well. Denies that she is having any headache or blurry vision. She is not having chest pain, pressure, leg swelling, paroxysmal nocturnal dyspnea or palpitations. Regarding her cholesterol she is compliant with her medication which includes Lipitor and Fenofibrate. She denies that she has any abdominal pain or muscle cramps on the medication. Regarding her diabetes she is treated with insulin as well as Januvia and Metformin. Does bring a blood sugar log with her today. Fasting readings are in the low 100's. Her ranges today are 99-120. She also has readings after lunch, dinner and at bedtime. These readings are generally in the 130's-150's range. She denies that she has difficulty with her blood sugars being too low. She says that typically the lowest they'll get is in the 70's or 80's. Overall she reports that she has been feeling well. ls eating fine. No issues with her bowel pattern. No constipation or blood stool. Sleeps well. Again she's not having any chest pain or breathing problems.

Chief Complaint Follow up of chronic medical issues.

History of Present Illness

Betty comes in today to follow up on her chronic medical issues which include hypertension, diabetes and hypercholesterolemia. She is fasting today and is due lab work. She does bring a blood glucose log with her. Her fasting blood sugar readings range from 91-132. After meals her ranges are 96-164. After lunch 122-170. After dinner and bedtime ranges from 118-211. She tells me that she does feel like she is doing well with her insulin regimen and is hopeful that her A1c will be better this time. Her only real concern today is that she's been having some cramps in her legs. Betty is not on any diuretic that would cause potassium wasting. She says that she really isn't sure if she drinks enough water or not but does try to eat a variety of foods. She has only recently noticed her legs sometimes feeling achy and tight and she thought that maybe her potassium was low.

PFSH

She denies that she's had any recent fever, chills or night sweats. No chronic fatigue. No nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, constipation or bloody stool. She reports having had a colonoscopy about eight years ago. She does not have chronic headaches, ringing in her ears or blurry vision. No chest pain, pressure palpitations, leg swelling or difficulty breathing.

Morning blood sugars are running in the 120-140 range. Lunch blood sugars are a bit higher in the 150's and she does occasionally have numbers over 200 at bedtime. She denies that she has any issues with low blood sugar readings. We did review her diabetic flow sheet and her Alc in June was 7.7.

Also after her last visit we added on some Norvasc for hypertension. She is taking her blood pressures at home and reports that typically she doesn't have a lot of trouble with them. It is a bit higher today she thinks because she is at the doctor and also because she's not taken her medications yet. She typically takes them around 6 am but didn't take them today because she is due fasting blood work.

Her only real concern today is that she's been having some pain in her left shoulder. She hasn't taken anything OTC because she isn't sure what she can take. She complains that the pain is mostly kind of along the outside of the shoulder, is achy, seems to get sore if she moves it a certain way and sometimes is pretty stiff first thing in the morning. She is able to use her arm overhead but says that sometimes it seems like it rubs or aches with overhead use. She doesn't have any numbness or tingling sensation down the left arm. Doesn't feel like her arm or grip strength is weak just kind of a tooth-achy pain at times.
